It keeps the same directory structure and deliverables as the previous runs, but with a tighter window and lighter pruning.

###############################################################################
# CHILE — Profit swings diagnostic with ECT
# VERY SHORT WINDOW: 1968–1975
#
# Purpose:
# - Identify Chile profit swings in the micro-window covering
#   the critical juncture around the Unidad Popular and the onset
#   of counter-revolution
# - Use a joint diagnostic:
#   (i) smoothed log-differential profitability
#   (ii) profit rate in level
# - Include ECT as a diagnostic layer for external imbalance pressure
# - Produce transparent CSV/RDS outputs and two figures
#
# Output root:
# - output/profitability_chile_diagnostic_short_very_19681975
#
# Directory structure:
# - csv/
# - figures/
# - rds/
###############################################################################

# ── 0. Packages ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
pkgs <- c("dplyr", "readr", "tibble", "zoo", "ggplot2", "janitor")
miss <- pkgs[!vapply(pkgs, requireNamespace, logical(1), quietly = TRUE)]
if (length(miss) > 0) install.packages(miss, repos = "https://cloud.r-project.org")
invisible(lapply(pkgs, library, character.only = TRUE))

# ── 1. Paths and controls ────────────────────────────────────────────────────
proj_root <- "C:/ReposGitHub/Capacity-Utilization-US_Chile"

path_d_rds <- file.path(
  proj_root, "output", "profitability_chile", "rds", "d_merged_profitability_chile.rds"
)

path_bundle_rds <- file.path(
  proj_root, "output", "profitability_chile", "rds", "analytical_bundle_chile.rds"
)

out_root <- file.path(
  proj_root, "output", "profitability_chile_diagnostic_short_very_19681975"
)
csv_dir  <- file.path(out_root, "csv")
fig_dir  <- file.path(out_root, "figures")
rds_dir  <- file.path(out_root, "rds")

dir.create(csv_dir, recursive = TRUE, showWarnings = FALSE)
dir.create(fig_dir, recursive = TRUE, showWarnings = FALSE)
dir.create(rds_dir, recursive = TRUE, showWarnings = FALSE)

analysis_year_min <- 1968L
analysis_year_max <- 1975L

# Carrier settings
level_var <- "r_diag_t"
log_var   <- "ln_r_diag_t"
ect_var   <- "ect"

# Signal settings
k_smooth     <- 3L
ect_smooth_k <- 3L
local_span   <- 1L

# Lighter pruning for micro-window
min_years_between_tp <- 1L
min_log_move         <- 0.01

# Figure settings

fig_height <- 7
fig_dpi    <- 320

# ── 2. Helpers ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
sign_eps <- function(x, eps = 1e-10) {
  ifelse(is.na(x) | abs(x) <= eps, 0L, ifelse(x > 0, 1L, -1L))
}

zsafe <- function(x) {
  s <- stats::sd(x, na.rm = TRUE)
  m <- mean(x, na.rm = TRUE)
  if (!is.finite(s) || s <= 0) return(rep(NA_real_, length(x)))
  (x - m) / s
}

load_profitability_panel <- function(path_d_rds, path_bundle_rds) {
  if (file.exists(path_d_rds)) {
    return(readRDS(path_d_rds))
  }

  if (file.exists(path_bundle_rds)) {
    b <- readRDS(path_bundle_rds)
    if (!("d" %in% names(b))) {
      stop("Bundle found, but object 'd' is missing.", call. = FALSE)
    }
    return(b$d)
  }

  stop(
    "Could not find either d_merged_profitability_chile.rds or analytical_bundle_chile.rds.",
    call. = FALSE
  )
}

locate_local_extremum <- function(year, level, i, type, span = 1L) {
  lo <- max(1L, i - span)
  hi <- min(length(level), i + span)
  win_idx <- lo:hi
  win_val <- level[win_idx]

  if (all(is.na(win_val))) {
    return(tibble::tibble(
      idx = i,
      year = year[i],
      value = level[i],
      type = type
    ))
  }

  j <- if (type == "peak") {
    win_idx[which.max(win_val)]
  } else {
    win_idx[which.min(win_val)]
  }

  tibble::tibble(
    idx = j,
    year = year[j],
    value = level[j],
    type = type
  )
}

compute_signal_table <- function(df, level_var, log_var, k_smooth,
                                 ect_var = "ect", ect_smooth_k = 3L) {
  if (!(level_var %in% names(df))) {
    stop("Missing level_var in input data: ", level_var, call. = FALSE)
  }
  if (!(ect_var %in% names(df))) {
    stop("Missing ect_var in input data: ", ect_var, call. = FALSE)
  }

  out <- df |>
    dplyr::arrange(year) |>
    dplyr::transmute(
      year,
      r_level = .data[[level_var]],
      ln_r    = if (log_var %in% names(df)) .data[[log_var]] else log(.data[[level_var]]),
      ect     = .data[[ect_var]]
    ) |>
    dplyr::mutate(
      dlog_r = ln_r - dplyr::lag(ln_r),
      dlog_r_smoothed = zoo::rollmean(dlog_r, k = k_smooth, fill = NA, align = "center"),
      ect_smoothed    = zoo::rollmean(ect, k = ect_smooth_k, fill = NA, align = "center")
    ) |>
    dplyr::mutate(
      dlog_r_z          = zsafe(dlog_r),
      dlog_r_smoothed_z = zsafe(dlog_r_smoothed),
      ect_z             = zsafe(ect),
      ect_smoothed_z    = zsafe(ect_smoothed)
    )

  out
}

compress_turning_points <- function(tp) {
  if (nrow(tp) <= 1) return(tp)

  keep <- vector("list", 0)
  current <- tp[1, , drop = FALSE]

  for (i in 2:nrow(tp)) {
    this <- tp[i, , drop = FALSE]

    if (this$type == current$type) {
      if (this$type == "peak"   && this$value > current$value) current <- this
      if (this$type == "trough" && this$value < current$value) current <- this
    } else {
      keep[[length(keep) + 1]] <- current
      current <- this
    }
  }

  keep[[length(keep) + 1]] <- current
  dplyr::bind_rows(keep) |>
    dplyr::arrange(idx)
}

find_tp_from_signal <- function(signal_tbl, signal_col, span = 1L, eps = 1e-10, method_name = "signal_rule") {
  year  <- signal_tbl$year
  level <- signal_tbl$r_level
  sig   <- signal_tbl[[signal_col]]

  out <- vector("list", 0)

  if (length(sig) < 3) {
    return(tibble::tibble(
      method = character(),
      signal_col = character(),
      signal_idx = integer(),
      signal_year = integer(),
      idx = integer(),
      year = integer(),
      value = numeric(),
      type = character(),
      signal_prev = numeric(),
      signal_curr = numeric(),
      signal_strength = numeric()
    ))
  }

  for (i in 2:(length(sig) - 1)) {
    if (is.na(sig[i - 1]) || is.na(sig[i])) next

    s_prev <- sign_eps(sig[i - 1], eps = eps)
    s_curr <- sign_eps(sig[i], eps = eps)

    if (s_prev > 0L && s_curr < 0L) {
      ext <- locate_local_extremum(year, level, i, "peak", span = span)
      out[[length(out) + 1]] <- tibble::tibble(
        method = method_name,
        signal_col = signal_col,
        signal_idx = i,
        signal_year = year[i],
        idx = ext$idx,
        year = ext$year,
        value = ext$value,
        type = ext$type,
        signal_prev = sig[i - 1],
        signal_curr = sig[i],
        signal_strength = abs(sig[i - 1]) + abs(sig[i])
      )
    } else if (s_prev < 0L && s_curr > 0L) {
      ext <- locate_local_extremum(year, level, i, "trough", span = span)
      out[[length(out) + 1]] <- tibble::tibble(
        method = method_name,
        signal_col = signal_col,
        signal_idx = i,
        signal_year = year[i],
        idx = ext$idx,
        year = ext$year,
        value = ext$value,
        type = ext$type,
        signal_prev = sig[i - 1],
        signal_curr = sig[i],
        signal_strength = abs(sig[i - 1]) + abs(sig[i])
      )
    }
  }

  if (length(out) == 0) {
    return(tibble::tibble(
      method = character(),
      signal_col = character(),
      signal_idx = integer(),
      signal_year = integer(),
      idx = integer(),
      year = integer(),
      value = numeric(),
      type = character(),
      signal_prev = numeric(),
      signal_curr = numeric(),
      signal_strength = numeric()
    ))
  }

  dplyr::bind_rows(out) |>
    dplyr::distinct(idx, .keep_all = TRUE) |>
    dplyr::arrange(idx)
}

find_tp_from_levels <- function(signal_tbl, span = 1L) {
  year  <- signal_tbl$year
  level <- signal_tbl$r_level

  out <- vector("list", 0)

  if (length(level) < 3) {
    return(tibble::tibble(
      method = character(),
      signal_col = character(),
      signal_idx = integer(),
      signal_year = integer(),
      idx = integer(),
      year = integer(),
      value = numeric(),
      type = character(),
      signal_prev = numeric(),
      signal_curr = numeric(),
      signal_strength = numeric()
    ))
  }

  for (i in 2:(length(level) - 1)) {
    if (is.na(level[i - 1]) || is.na(level[i]) || is.na(level[i + 1])) next

    if (level[i - 1] < level[i] && level[i] > level[i + 1]) {
      ext <- locate_local_extremum(year, level, i, "peak", span = span)
      out[[length(out) + 1]] <- tibble::tibble(
        method = "level_extrema",
        signal_col = "r_level",
        signal_idx = i,
        signal_year = year[i],
        idx = ext$idx,
        year = ext$year,
        value = ext$value,
        type = ext$type,
        signal_prev = NA_real_,
        signal_curr = NA_real_,
        signal_strength = NA_real_
      )
    } else if (level[i - 1] > level[i] && level[i] < level[i + 1]) {
      ext <- locate_local_extremum(year, level, i, "trough", span = span)
      out[[length(out) + 1]] <- tibble::tibble(
        method = "level_extrema",
        signal_col = "r_level",
        signal_idx = i,
        signal_year = year[i],
        idx = ext$idx,
        year = ext$year,
        value = ext$value,
        type = ext$type,
        signal_prev = NA_real_,
        signal_curr = NA_real_,
        signal_strength = NA_real_
      )
    }
  }

  if (length(out) == 0) {
    return(tibble::tibble(
      method = character(),
      signal_col = character(),
      signal_idx = integer(),
      signal_year = integer(),
      idx = integer(),
      year = integer(),
      value = numeric(),
      type = character(),
      signal_prev = numeric(),
      signal_curr = numeric(),
      signal_strength = numeric()
    ))
  }

  dplyr::bind_rows(out) |>
    dplyr::distinct(idx, .keep_all = TRUE) |>
    dplyr::arrange(idx)
}

prune_turning_points_joint <- function(tp, signal_tbl, min_years = 1L, min_log_move = 0.01) {
  if (nrow(tp) <= 1) return(tp)

  level <- signal_tbl$r_level
  log_level <- log(level)
  out <- tp

  repeat {
    if (nrow(out) <= 1) break

    dur <- diff(out$year)
    amp_log <- abs(diff(log_level[out$idx]))
    weak <- which(dur < min_years | amp_log < min_log_move)

    if (length(weak) == 0) break

    k <- weak[1]

    if (k == 1) {
      out <- out[-2, , drop = FALSE]
    } else if (k == nrow(out) - 1) {
      out <- out[-k, , drop = FALSE]
    } else {
      left_idx  <- out$idx[k - 1]
      a_idx     <- out$idx[k]
      b_idx     <- out$idx[k + 1]
      right_idx <- out$idx[k + 2]

      move_drop_left  <- abs(log_level[b_idx] - log_level[left_idx])
      move_drop_right <- abs(log_level[right_idx] - log_level[a_idx])

      if (move_drop_left >= move_drop_right) {
        out <- out[-k, , drop = FALSE]
      } else {
        out <- out[-(k + 1), , drop = FALSE]
      }
    }

    out <- compress_turning_points(out)
  }

  out
}

make_boundary_only_tp <- function(signal_tbl) {
  level_first <- signal_tbl$r_level[1]
  level_last  <- signal_tbl$r_level[nrow(signal_tbl)]

  start_type <- if (level_last >= level_first) "trough" else "peak"
  end_type   <- if (start_type == "trough") "peak" else "trough"

  tibble::tibble(
    method = "boundary_only",
    signal_col = NA_character_,
    signal_idx = c(NA_integer_, NA_integer_),
    signal_year = c(NA_integer_, NA_integer_),
    idx = c(1L, nrow(signal_tbl)),
    year = c(signal_tbl$year[1], signal_tbl$year[nrow(signal_tbl)]),
    value = c(signal_tbl$r_level[1], signal_tbl$r_level[nrow(signal_tbl)]),
    type = c(start_type, end_type),
    signal_prev = c(NA_real_, NA_real_),
    signal_curr = c(NA_real_, NA_real_),
    signal_strength = c(NA_real_, NA_real_)
  )
}

add_boundaries_keep_rhs <- function(tp, signal_tbl) {
  if (nrow(tp) == 0) {
    return(make_boundary_only_tp(signal_tbl))
  }

  first_type <- if (tp$type[1] == "peak") "trough" else "peak"
  last_type  <- if (tp$type[nrow(tp)] == "peak") "trough" else "peak"

  start_row <- tibble::tibble(
    method = "boundary",
    signal_col = NA_character_,
    signal_idx = NA_integer_,
    signal_year = NA_integer_,
    idx = 1L,
    year = signal_tbl$year[1],
    value = signal_tbl$r_level[1],
    type = first_type,
    signal_prev = NA_real_,
    signal_curr = NA_real_,
    signal_strength = NA_real_
  )

  end_row <- tibble::tibble(
    method = "boundary",
    signal_col = NA_character_,
    signal_idx = NA_integer_,
    signal_year = NA_integer_,
    idx = nrow(signal_tbl),
    year = signal_tbl$year[nrow(signal_tbl)],
    value = signal_tbl$r_level[nrow(signal_tbl)],
    type = last_type,
    signal_prev = NA_real_,
    signal_curr = NA_real_,
    signal_strength = NA_real_
  )

  dplyr::bind_rows(start_row, tp, end_row) |>
    dplyr::arrange(idx) |>
    compress_turning_points()
}

build_swing_table <- function(tp_bounds, signal_tbl) {
  if (nrow(tp_bounds) < 2) return(tibble::tibble())

  out <- vector("list", nrow(tp_bounds) - 1)

  for (i in seq_len(nrow(tp_bounds) - 1)) {
    idx0 <- tp_bounds$idx[i]
    idx1 <- tp_bounds$idx[i + 1]

    y0 <- tp_bounds$year[i]
    y1 <- tp_bounds$year[i + 1]

    r0  <- signal_tbl$r_level[idx0]
    r1  <- signal_tbl$r_level[idx1]
    ln0 <- signal_tbl$ln_r[idx0]
    ln1 <- signal_tbl$ln_r[idx1]

    ect0 <- signal_tbl$ect[idx0]
    ect1 <- signal_tbl$ect[idx1]
    ect_avg <- mean(signal_tbl$ect[idx0:idx1], na.rm = TRUE)
    ect_sm_avg <- mean(signal_tbl$ect_smoothed[idx0:idx1], na.rm = TRUE)

    dur <- y1 - y0

    out[[i]] <- tibble::tibble(
      swing_id = i,
      start_year = y0,
      end_year = y1,
      start_type = tp_bounds$type[i],
      end_type   = tp_bounds$type[i + 1],
      direction  = paste0(tp_bounds$type[i], "_to_", tp_bounds$type[i + 1]),
      duration_years = dur,
      start_r = r0,
      end_r   = r1,
      amplitude_pct = 100 * (r1 / r0 - 1),
      amplitude_log = ln1 - ln0,
      pace_pct_per_year = ifelse(dur > 0, 100 * ((r1 / r0)^(1 / dur) - 1), NA_real_),
      pace_log_per_year = ifelse(dur > 0, (ln1 - ln0) / dur, NA_real_),
      ect_start = ect0,
      ect_end   = ect1,
      ect_avg   = ect_avg,
      ect_smoothed_avg = ect_sm_avg,
      boundary_only = all(tp_bounds$method == "boundary_only"),
      rhs_terminal_window = (i == (nrow(tp_bounds) - 1))
    )
  }

  dplyr::bind_rows(out)
}

plot_joint_diagnostic <- function(signal_tbl, tp_used, out_png, out_pdf, title_txt = NULL) {
  level <- signal_tbl$r_level
  sig   <- signal_tbl$dlog_r_smoothed

  level_center <- mean(level, na.rm = TRUE)
  sig_range <- range(sig, na.rm = TRUE)
  lvl_range <- range(level, na.rm = TRUE)

  if (!all(is.finite(sig_range)) || diff(sig_range) == 0) {
    scale_fac <- 1
  } else {
    scale_fac <- 0.85 * diff(lvl_range) / diff(sig_range)
  }

  signal_plot <- signal_tbl |>
    dplyr::mutate(
      dlog_plot = level_center + dlog_r_smoothed * scale_fac
    )

  tp_plot <- tp_used |>
    dplyr::filter(!method %in% c("boundary", "boundary_only")) |>
    dplyr::transmute(
      year,
      r_level = value,
      type
    )

  p <- ggplot(signal_plot, aes(x = year)) +
    geom_hline(yintercept = level_center, linetype = "dotted", linewidth = 0.4) +
    geom_line(aes(y = r_level), linewidth = 1.1) +
    geom_line(aes(y = dlog_plot), linetype = "dashed", linewidth = 0.9) +
    geom_point(
      data = dplyr::filter(tp_plot, type == "peak"),
      aes(y = r_level, shape = type),
      size = 3.2, stroke = 0.8, fill = NA
    ) +
    geom_point(
      data = dplyr::filter(tp_plot, type == "trough"),
      aes(y = r_level, shape = type),
      size = 3.2, stroke = 0.8, fill = NA
    ) +
    scale_shape_manual(values = c(peak = 24, trough = 25)) +
    scale_y_continuous(
      name = "profit rate",
      sec.axis = sec_axis(
        trans = ~ (. - level_center) / scale_fac,
        name = "smoothed Δ log profitability"
      )
    ) +
    labs(
      x = NULL,
      title = title_txt,
      shape = NULL
    ) +
    theme_minimal(base_size = 13) +
    theme(
      panel.grid.minor = element_blank(),
      legend.position = "bottom"
    )

  ggsave(out_png, p, width = fig_width, height = fig_height, dpi = fig_dpi)
  ggsave(out_pdf, p, width = fig_width, height = fig_height)

  invisible(p)
}

plot_ect_diagnostic <- function(signal_tbl, tp_used, out_png, out_pdf, title_txt = NULL) {
  tp_vlines <- tp_used |>
    dplyr::filter(!method %in% c("boundary", "boundary_only"))

  p <- ggplot(signal_tbl, aes(x = year)) +
    geom_hline(yintercept = 0, linetype = "dotted", linewidth = 0.4) +
    geom_line(aes(y = dlog_r_smoothed_z, linetype = "Smoothed Δlog profitability (z)"), linewidth = 1.0) +
    geom_line(aes(y = ect_smoothed_z, linetype = "ECT external imbalance (z)"), linewidth = 1.0) +
    geom_vline(
      data = tp_vlines,
      aes(xintercept = year),
      linewidth = 0.35,
      alpha = 0.45
    ) +
    scale_linetype_manual(values = c(
      "Smoothed Δlog profitability (z)" = "dashed",
      "ECT external imbalance (z)" = "solid"
    )) +
    labs(
      x = NULL,
      y = "standardized diagnostic scale",
      title = title_txt,
      linetype = NULL
    ) +
    theme_minimal(base_size = 13) +
    theme(
      panel.grid.minor = element_blank(),
      legend.position = "bottom"
    )

  ggsave(out_png, p, width = fig_width, height = fig_height, dpi = fig_dpi)
  ggsave(out_pdf, p, width = fig_width, height = fig_height)

  invisible(p)
}

# ── 3. Load data ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
d <- load_profitability_panel(path_d_rds, path_bundle_rds)

required_vars <- c("year", level_var, ect_var)
miss_vars <- required_vars[!required_vars %in% names(d)]
if (length(miss_vars) > 0) {
  stop("Missing required variable(s): ", paste(miss_vars, collapse = ", "), call. = FALSE)
}

d <- d |>
  dplyr::filter(year >= analysis_year_min, year <= analysis_year_max) |>
  dplyr::arrange(year)

if (!(log_var %in% names(d))) {
  d[[log_var]] <- log(d[[level_var]])
}

if (any(!is.finite(d[[level_var]]) | d[[level_var]] <= 0, na.rm = TRUE)) {
  stop("Profit-rate level series contains non-positive or non-finite values.", call. = FALSE)
}

# ── 4. Compute signals ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────
signal_tbl <- compute_signal_table(
  df = d,
  level_var = level_var,
  log_var = log_var,
  k_smooth = k_smooth,
  ect_var = ect_var,
  ect_smooth_k = ect_smooth_k
)

# ── 5. Detection ladder ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────
tp_candidates_primary <- find_tp_from_signal(
  signal_tbl = signal_tbl,
  signal_col = "dlog_r_smoothed",
  span = local_span,
  method_name = "smoothed_dlog_rule"
) |>
  compress_turning_points()

tp_candidates_raw <- find_tp_from_signal(
  signal_tbl = signal_tbl,
  signal_col = "dlog_r",
  span = local_span,
  method_name = "raw_dlog_rule"
) |>
  compress_turning_points()

tp_candidates_level <- find_tp_from_levels(
  signal_tbl = signal_tbl,
  span = local_span
) |>
  compress_turning_points()

tp_candidates_used <- tp_candidates_primary
candidate_method_used <- "smoothed_dlog_rule"

if (nrow(tp_candidates_used) == 0 && nrow(tp_candidates_raw) > 0) {
  tp_candidates_used <- tp_candidates_raw
  candidate_method_used <- "raw_dlog_rule"
}

if (nrow(tp_candidates_used) == 0 && nrow(tp_candidates_level) > 0) {
  tp_candidates_used <- tp_candidates_level
  candidate_method_used <- "level_extrema"
}

tp_final_pruned <- if (nrow(tp_candidates_used) > 0) {
  prune_turning_points_joint(
    tp = tp_candidates_used,
    signal_tbl = signal_tbl,
    min_years = min_years_between_tp,
    min_log_move = min_log_move
  ) |>
    compress_turning_points()
} else {
  tp_candidates_used
}

tp_used <- tp_final_pruned
used_boundary_only <- FALSE

if (nrow(tp_used) == 0) {
  tp_used <- make_boundary_only_tp(signal_tbl)
  used_boundary_only <- TRUE
}

tp_bounds <- if (used_boundary_only) {
  tp_used
} else {
  add_boundaries_keep_rhs(
    tp = tp_used,
    signal_tbl = signal_tbl
  )
}

swings_tbl <- build_swing_table(
  tp_bounds = tp_bounds,
  signal_tbl = signal_tbl
)

tp_status <- tibble::tibble(
  level_var = level_var,
  log_var = log_var,
  ect_var = ect_var,
  n_candidates_primary = nrow(tp_candidates_primary),
  n_candidates_raw = nrow(tp_candidates_raw),
  n_candidates_level = nrow(tp_candidates_level),
  candidate_method_used = candidate_method_used,
  n_candidates_used = nrow(tp_candidates_used),
  n_after_prune = nrow(tp_final_pruned),
  used_boundary_only = used_boundary_only
)

config_tbl <- tibble::tibble(
  analysis_year_min = analysis_year_min,
  analysis_year_max = analysis_year_max,
  level_var = level_var,
  log_var = log_var,
  ect_var = ect_var,
  k_smooth = k_smooth,
  ect_smooth_k = ect_smooth_k,
  local_span = local_span,
  min_years_between_tp = min_years_between_tp,
  min_log_move = min_log_move
)

readr::write_csv(tp_candidates_used, file.path(csv_dir, "turning_points_candidates_used_chile_profit_swings_short_very_19681975.csv"))
readr::write_csv(tp_final_pruned, file.path(csv_dir, "turning_points_final_pruned_chile_profit_swings_short_very_19681975.csv"))
readr::write_csv(tp_used, file.path(csv_dir, "turning_points_used_chile_profit_swings_short_very_19681975.csv"))
readr::write_csv(tp_bounds, file.path(csv_dir, "turning_points_with_boundaries_chile_profit_swings_short_very_19681975.csv"))
readr::write_csv(swings_tbl, file.path(csv_dir, "profit_swings_joint_diagnostic_chile_short_very_19681975.csv"))

saveRDS(config_tbl, file.path(rds_dir, "diagnostic_config_chile_profit_swings_short_very_19681975.rds"))
saveRDS(tp_status, file.path(rds_dir, "turning_points_status_chile_profit_swings_short_very_19681975.rds"))
saveRDS(signal_tbl, file.path(rds_dir, "signal_table_chile_profit_swings_short_very_19681975.rds"))
saveRDS(tp_candidates_primary, file.path(rds_dir, "turning_points_candidates_primary_chile_profit_swings_short_very_19681975.rds"))
saveRDS(tp_candidates_raw, file.path(rds_dir, "turning_points_candidates_raw_chile_profit_swings_short_very_19681975.rds"))
saveRDS(tp_candidates_level, file.path(rds_dir, "turning_points_candidates_level_chile_profit_swings_short_very_19681975.rds"))
saveRDS(tp_candidates_used, file.path(rds_dir, "turning_points_candidates_used_chile_profit_swings_short_very_19681975.rds"))
saveRDS(tp_final_pruned, file.path(rds_dir, "turning_points_final_pruned_chile_profit_swings_short_very_19681975.rds"))
saveRDS(tp_used, file.path(rds_dir, "turning_points_used_chile_profit_swings_short_very_19681975.rds"))
saveRDS(tp_bounds, file.path(rds_dir, "turning_points_with_boundaries_chile_profit_swings_short_very_19681975.rds"))
saveRDS(swings_tbl, file.path(rds_dir, "profit_swings_joint_diagnostic_chile_short_very_19681975.rds"))

)

Thought for 38s
This very-short diagnostic is the first one that really bites 🎯

The main result is sharp:

peak: 1969

trough: 1972

So the micro-window is reading the critical juncture as:

1968–1969: final upswing

1969–1972: major contraction

1972–1975: rebound

And the amplitudes are not trivial:

1968–1969: about +8.3%

1969–1972: about -37.9%

1972–1975: about +29.1%

That is a strong crisis sequence.

But there are three important qualifications.

First, in this window the algorithm is not using the primary smoothed rule. It fell back to the raw Δlog(r) rule. That is not bad, but it tells you the micro-window is too short and sparse for the smoothed rule to dominate cleanly. So this figure is more delicate than the 1957–1978 one.

Second, the last rebound 1972–1975 is marked as the RHS terminal swing. That means it is analytically useful, but still incomplete by construction. You should treat it as “rebound underway by the end of the observed window,” not as a fully matured restorative phase.

Third, and this is crucial: your signal table for this run has no 1974 observation. The sequence goes 1968, 1969, 1970, 1971, 1972, 1973, 1975. So the rebound from 1972 to 1975 is spanning a gap. That does not invalidate the result, but it absolutely weakens any attempt to narrate the immediate post-coup trajectory too precisely from this window alone.

Substantively, the reading is now much clearer than before.

The profit-rate figure says:

the profitability crest is before the UP government fully consolidates,

the real collapse is concentrated into 1969–1972,

and the low point is reached in 1972, not only after the coup.

That is important because it gives you strong support for saying that the crisis intensifies inside the UP sequence rather than beginning only in the aftermath.

At the same time, this micro-diagnostic does not show a distinct “UP offset in 1971” as a separate turning point. What it shows instead is:

a decline from the 1969 peak into 1971,

then a sharper fall into the 1972 trough.

So the evidence here is better for:

reversal clearly underway by 1972

than for:

a separate, strong profitability offset in 1971

Now look at the ECT panel. This is where the interpretation gets stronger.

During the 1969–1972 contraction, ECT rises from roughly -6.30 to -6.23. In other words, external imbalance does not worsen during that exact contraction segment; it slightly eases.

But during the 1972–1975 rebound, average ECT worsens materially, and by 1975 the ECT level is much more negative than at the trough. So the post-1972 profitability recovery is happening under deteriorating external disequilibrium.

That is the real theoretical payoff here:

the crisis trough is visible in 1972

the subsequent profitability rebound does not coincide with external repair

instead, it unfolds while the balance-of-payments constraint becomes harsher

So the rebound is best read as a fragile or forced offset, not as stabilization.

That gives you a very useful layered presentation logic.

I would present the three diagnostics like this:

The medium run gives the long arc.

The 1957–1978 short run gives the politically readable sequence:
long-sixties rise, crisis corridor, and counter-revolutionary onset.

The 1968–1975 very-short run gives the crisis-core message:

1969 peak

1972 trough

post-1972 rebound under worsening external imbalance

That last clause is the killer line.

So the final interpretive judgment is:

This micro-window supports:

a major profitability reversal culminating in 1972

a post-trough rebound

that rebound occurring under worse ECT conditions

It does not fully support:

a clean, distinct “1971 profitability offset” as its own swing phase

And because 1974 is missing, I would avoid overclaiming the immediate post-coup year-by-year path from this figure alone.

My recommendation on presentation is now pretty settled:

use 1957–1978 as the main short-run figure in the chapter

use 1968–1975 as the inset / zoom figure for the critical juncture

interpret the micro-window not as “three fully separate political regimes,” but as:
pre-crisis crest → 1972 breakdown → fragile rebound under external deterioration

If you want, the next clean move is to draft a compact interpretive paragraph that places the medium-run, short-run, and very-short-run diagnostics into one coherent narrative for the chapter.

Thought for 51s
Yes. Two separate points.

On the first one: yes, the micro-window is showing a rebound in the growth rate of profitability before it shows a full restoration in levels.

From the signal table for 1968–1975:

1970 raw dlog_r = -0.0388

1971 raw dlog_r = -0.0615

1972 raw dlog_r = -0.3766

1973 raw dlog_r = +0.3106

1975 raw dlog_r = -0.0553

And the level profit rate goes:

1969 = 0.1202

1970 = 0.1157

1971 = 0.1088

1972 = 0.0746

1973 = 0.1018

1975 = 0.0963

So the exact reading is:

there is a clear rebound in profitability growth after the 1972 collapse,

and there is also a level rebound from 0.0746 in 1972 to 0.1018 in 1973,

but that rebound does not restore the pre-crisis crest of 1969 = 0.1202,

and by 1975 the level is still below 1973.

So this is not just “rebound in growth with no rebound in levels.” It is:

rebound in growth and partial rebound in levels, without full restoration of the prior profitability regime.

That is exactly the sort of pattern that is compatible with a temporary stabilization under fragility.

I would still be careful with the phrase wage-led stabilization. This figure alone does not identify the regime as wage-led. It identifies:

a collapse into 1972,

a partial recovery after the trough,

and no full restoration of the previous level regime.

To call it wage-led, you need to check the distributive side directly:

wsh / omega_t

pi_t

ideally the decomposition terms, especially the distributive and utilization contributions.

So the safer statement is:

the diagnostic is consistent with a short-lived stabilization attempt with high fragility, but not sufficient on its own to classify that stabilization as wage-led.

And the fragility part is strengthened by the ECT panel, because the rebound is occurring while the external situation is not being durably repaired.

Now the second point: yes, 1974 absolutely should be audited.

It is not a cosmetic issue. In this micro-window, the data go:

1968, 1969, 1970, 1971, 1972, 1973, 1975

So the last swing is spanning a missing year. That weakens any very precise interpretation of the immediate post-coup transition.

My guess is that 1974 is getting lost upstream in the merged panel, not in the diagnostic code itself. The diagnostic script just filters the already built d object. So if 1974 is absent there, the problem is in the analytical core inputs or splice.

missing theta_t / post-1974 splice issue,

missing capital or accounting variable in acc,

Thought for 39s
Yes — this is almost certainly an upstream splice cut, not a plotting problem.

The fact that d |> filter(year %in% 1973:1975) returns 1973 and 1975 but not 1974 means the row is already missing before the diagnostic code sees it.

The most likely cut is here in the analytical core:

# Stage 1 ECT
ect_isi  <- extract_stage1_ect(stage1_master, "ISI1931_1973")
ect_post <- extract_stage1_ect(stage1_master, "POST1974")

isi_part <- theta_isi |>
  dplyr::select(year, regime_code, theta_r1, theta_r2, theta_active) |>
  dplyr::left_join(ect_isi, by = "year") |>
  dplyr::mutate(true_sample = "ISI1931_1973")

post_part <- theta_post |>
  dplyr::select(year, regime_code, theta_r1, theta_r2, theta_active) |>
  dplyr::left_join(ect_post, by = "year") |>
  dplyr::mutate(true_sample = "POST1974")

ts_splice <- dplyr::bind_rows(isi_part, post_part) |>
  dplyr::filter(year >= 1932, year <= 2010) |>
  dplyr::arrange(year) |>
  dplyr::left_join(core, by = "year")
So the cut is probably happening in one of these two source objects:

theta_post

ect_post

or in the way the post sample was estimated upstream.

My bet is this:

POST1974 is the sample label, but the first usable estimated observation is 1975.

That would happen very naturally if the Stage 1 / Stage 2 post-sample machinery loses the first year because of lag structure or how the ECT series is exported.

What to check now
Run this exactly in the analytical core session, before ts_splice is built:

theta_isi  |> dplyr::filter(year %in% 1973:1975)
theta_post |> dplyr::filter(year %in% 1973:1975)

ect_isi    |> dplyr::filter(year %in% 1973:1975)
ect_post   |> dplyr::filter(year %in% 1973:1975)

isi_part   |> dplyr::filter(year %in% 1973:1975)
post_part  |> dplyr::filter(year %in% 1973:1975)
That will tell you immediately whether:

theta_post starts at 1975,

or ect_post starts at 1975,

or both.

The key interpretation
If theta_post itself starts at 1975, then the cut is not in the builder logic.
It is in the upstream post-sample results object.

If theta_post contains 1974 but post_part loses it after the left_join(ect_post, by = "year"), then the issue is in ect_post availability or later filtering.

If both contain 1974, then we have to inspect ts_splice and later merges, but from what you pasted, the most likely culprit is the sample handoff itself.

Should we patch the builder now?
Not blindly.

Because 1974 is a transition year, there are two distinct cases:

Case A. 1974 is genuinely unavailable from the post structural estimation
Then forcing it into ts_splice as if it were an estimated post-sample row would be analytically sloppy.

Case B. 1974 should be there but got dropped by a coding cut
Then yes, patch it.

If you want a descriptive continuity patch
If your goal is to keep 1974 in the profitability descriptive panel, even if it is structurally transitional, then the right place to patch is after ts_splice is created and before base is built.

That patch should only be used if you explicitly accept 1974 as a transition-year descriptive row, not a clean sample-estimated row.

Use this:

# ---- transition-year continuity patch for 1974 ----
if (!1974 %in% ts_splice$year) {
  row_1973 <- ts_splice |> dplyr::filter(year == 1973)
  row_1975 <- ts_splice |> dplyr::filter(year == 1975)

  if (nrow(row_1973) == 1 && nrow(row_1975) == 1) {
    row_1974 <- row_1975
    row_1974$year <- 1974
    row_1974$true_sample <- "TRANSITION_1974"

    # simple midpoint bridge for structural objects
    row_1974$theta_active <- mean(c(row_1973$theta_active, row_1975$theta_active), na.rm = TRUE)
    row_1974$ECT          <- mean(c(row_1973$ECT, row_1975$ECT), na.rm = TRUE)
    row_1974$y            <- mean(c(row_1973$y, row_1975$y), na.rm = TRUE)
    row_1974$k_nr         <- mean(c(row_1973$k_nr, row_1975$k_nr), na.rm = TRUE)

    ts_splice <- dplyr::bind_rows(ts_splice, row_1974) |>
      dplyr::arrange(year)
  }
}
My recommendation
First do the audit above.
Do not patch until you know whether the absence of 1974 is:

an upstream estimation feature, or

a coding drop.

But yes — your instinct is right:

this is a cut issue in the analytical core source handoff, not a figure issue.

Thought for 12s
Exactly. The cut is now identified cleanly. 🔧

1974 is missing because:

ect_post does include 1974

theta_post does not include 1974

post_part is built from theta_post and then left_join(ect_post, by = "year")

So this line is the effective drop point:

post_part <- theta_post |>
  dplyr::select(year, regime_code, theta_r1, theta_r2, theta_active) |>
  dplyr::left_join(ect_post, by = "year") |>
  dplyr::mutate(true_sample = "POST1974")
Because left_join() keeps the years from the left-hand table, 1974 disappears there since theta_post starts at 1975.

So the issue is not in ect_post, and not in the diagnostic code.
It is an upstream cut in the structural post sample, specifically in theta_post.

The logic is:

theta_isi ends at 1973

theta_post begins at 1975

therefore the splice leaves a structural hole in 1974

That means 1974 is currently a true missing bridge year in the analytical core.

What this implies
You now have two valid paths.

1. Strict structural path
Do not invent 1974.
Treat it as unavailable from the post structural estimation and keep the hole explicit.

This is the cleanest option if you want to preserve strict comparability of estimated structural objects.

2. Descriptive continuity path
Insert a transition-year bridge row for 1974 in the analytical core, only for descriptive profitability diagnostics.

This is the better option if your purpose is historical narration of the coup/aftermath sequence.

Given your current goal, I think you want path 2.

Exact patch place
CODE: analytical core

PLACE: immediately after ts_splice is created and before this line:

if (any(!is.finite(ts_splice$theta_active))) stop("Spliced panel has missing theta_active values.", call. = FALSE)
So patch right after:

ts_splice <- dplyr::bind_rows(isi_part, post_part) |>
  dplyr::filter(year >= 1932, year <= 2010) |>
  dplyr::arrange(year) |>
  dplyr::left_join(core, by = "year") |>
  dplyr::mutate(
    regime_code = factor(regime_code, levels = c("low_ect_side", "high_ect_side")),
    dlog_k_nr = c(NA_real_, diff(k_nr))
  )
Patch code
# ---- transition-year continuity patch for 1974 ----
if (!1974 %in% ts_splice$year) {
  row_1973 <- ts_splice |> dplyr::filter(year == 1973)
  row_1975 <- ts_splice |> dplyr::filter(year == 1975)

  if (nrow(row_1973) == 1 && nrow(row_1975) == 1) {
    row_1974 <- row_1975

    row_1974$year <- 1974
    row_1974$true_sample <- "TRANSITION_1974"

    # bridge structural objects across the splice
    row_1974$theta_active <- mean(c(row_1973$theta_active, row_1975$theta_active), na.rm = TRUE)
    row_1974$ECT          <- dplyr::coalesce(
      ect_post |> dplyr::filter(year == 1974) |> dplyr::pull(ECT),
      mean(c(row_1973$ECT, row_1975$ECT), na.rm = TRUE)
    )
    row_1974$y            <- mean(c(row_1973$y, row_1975$y), na.rm = TRUE)
    row_1974$k_nr         <- mean(c(row_1973$k_nr, row_1975$k_nr), na.rm = TRUE)

    ts_splice <- dplyr::bind_rows(ts_splice, row_1974) |>
      dplyr::arrange(year) |>
      dplyr::mutate(
        regime_code = factor(regime_code, levels = c("low_ect_side", "high_ect_side")),
        dlog_k_nr = c(NA_real_, diff(k_nr))
      )
  }
}
Why this version is the right one
I changed one thing from the earlier generic bridge:

for ECT, do not interpolate if you already have the observed ect_post value for 1974

use the actual available ect_post[1974]

So this patch is:

bridged for theta_active

observed for ECT

bridged for y and k_nr

That is the best descriptive compromise.

Recommended label in interpretation
If you use this patch, treat 1974 as:

transition-year descriptive bridge, not a fully estimated structural regime row

That phrasing keeps the method honest.

Bottom line
The cut is caused by theta_post, not ect_post.

Problem source: theta_post starts in 1975

Drop point: post_part <- theta_post |> ... |> left_join(ect_post, ...)

Patch location: analytical core, right after ts_splice creation

Best patch: add a bridged 1974 row as TRANSITION_1974

Once you rerun the core with that patch, the 1968–1975 diagnostic should become much more interpretable for the immediate post-coup sequence.

Thought for 10s
Yes.

What I’m suggesting is not to pretend 1974 was estimated by the post sample. It is to insert 1974 as an explicit transition-year bridge between the last ISI structural row in 1973 and the first post structural row in 1975.

So, conceptually:

1973 = last estimated ISI-side row

1975 = first estimated post-1974 row

1974 = bridged transition row, used for descriptive continuity

That means:

theta_active(1974) would be spliced/interpolated between 1973 and 1975

ECT(1974) should use the observed value you already have

y and k_nr can be bridged for continuity

true_sample should be labeled something like "TRANSITION_1974"

So yes, the logic is:

splice 1974 as a transition between both regimes

But with one crucial caveat:

only for the descriptive profitability/diagnostic layer, not as if it were a clean estimated structural regime observation.

That is the honest way to do it.

If you want strict structural purity, then you leave 1974 missing and explicitly say the post structural object starts in 1975. But if your goal is to narrate the coup/aftermath sequence in the diagnostic figures, then a bridged 1974 is the better choice.

My recommendation is:

keep the bridged 1974 in the analytical core descriptive panel

label it clearly as transition

do not treat it as a formally estimated post-regime row

That gives you continuity without methodological cosplay 😄

Exact patch to insert there
# ---- transition-year continuity patch for 1974 ----
if (!1974 %in% ts_splice$year) {
  row_1973 <- ts_splice |> dplyr::filter(year == 1973)
  row_1975 <- ts_splice |> dplyr::filter(year == 1975)

  if (nrow(row_1973) == 1 && nrow(row_1975) == 1) {
    row_1974 <- row_1975

    row_1974$year <- 1974
    row_1974$true_sample <- "TRANSITION_1974"

    row_1974$theta_active <- mean(c(row_1973$theta_active, row_1975$theta_active), na.rm = TRUE)
    row_1974$ECT <- dplyr::coalesce(
      ect_post |> dplyr::filter(year == 1974) |> dplyr::pull(ECT),
      mean(c(row_1973$ECT, row_1975$ECT), na.rm = TRUE)
    )
    row_1974$y <- mean(c(row_1973$y, row_1975$y), na.rm = TRUE)
    row_1974$k_nr <- mean(c(row_1973$k_nr, row_1975$k_nr), na.rm = TRUE)

    ts_splice <- dplyr::bind_rows(ts_splice, row_1974) |>
      dplyr::arrange(year) |>
      dplyr::mutate(
        regime_code = factor(regime_code, levels = c("low_ect_side", "high_ect_side")),
        dlog_k_nr = c(NA_real_, diff(k_nr))
      )
  }
}

Thought for 11s
Good. The runs completed. Those warnings are not breaking the diagnostics.

What they mean:

The “Removed 3 rows” warnings come from the centered rolling mean. With k = 3, the smoothed series necessarily loses edge observations, so geom_line() drops those NA rows. That is expected.

The “Removed 2 rows” warnings in the ECT figure are the same logic: one smoothed series plus the restricted window creates a couple of edge NAs. Also expected.

The only ugly warning is the Unicode one:

conversion failure on 'Δ' ...

That is just a label-rendering issue in the plotting device on Windows. The figures are still generated, but the delta symbol may fail in the PDF text layer.

Use this label patch in all three diagnostic scripts:

# In plot_joint_diagnostic()
name = "smoothed dlog profitability"

# In plot_ect_diagnostic()
geom_line(aes(y = dlog_r_smoothed_z, linetype = "Smoothed dlog profitability (z)"), linewidth = 1.0)

scale_linetype_manual(values = c(
  "Smoothed dlog profitability (z)" = "dashed",
  "ECT external imbalance (z)" = "solid"
))
So, operationally:

edge-row warnings = normal

Unicode delta warning = cosmetic

Thought for 1m 35s
Yes. The clean way to reconcile the strategy is to stop treating profitability, recapitalization, and dysfunctionality as separate result families and instead turn them into a single period-state architecture.

The short version is this: the unit of interpretation should no longer be the individual indicator. It should be the period.

I would build the results package around a nested period panel with two layers.

First, a primary periodization for the chapter-facing results:
1961–69, 1969–72, 1972–74, 1974–76, 1976–78.

Second, a micro periodization only inside the critical corridor:
1969–72, 1972–74, 1974–75.

That gives you one stable backbone and one zoomed crisis core.

Then, for each period, collapse the continuous diagnostics into a common set of period features. The right bundle is:

profitability dynamics

recapitalization dynamics

dysfunctionality dynamics

external disequilibrium pressure

Concretely, I would compute for each period:

profit_sign = sign of profitability movement
profit_restoration = whether end-of-period profitability recovers prior peak
chi_level = average recapitalization ratio
chi_change = change in recapitalization ratio within the period
dys_level = average dysfunctionality index
offset_share = average S_off
fragility = average F_rev
ext_stress = average or end-of-period ECT pressure
ext_worsening = whether ECT deteriorates within the period

That gives you one row per period and turns the whole section into something Boolean-testable.

Then convert those into crisp qualitative conditions. I would use a threshold book once, chapter-wide, and keep it fixed. Not one threshold set for each zoom window. Otherwise the booleans start shape-shifting like guilty witnesses.

A very workable Boolean dictionary is:

PROF_DOWN = profitability falls over the period
PROF_UP = profitability rises over the period
RESTORE_FAIL = profitability rises but does not recover the previous peak
CHI_HIGH = average chi above reference threshold
CHI_RISING = delta chi > 0
RECAP_FAIL = low chi or rising chi without profitability restoration
DYS_HIGH = dysfunctionality above threshold
OFF_HIGH = offsetting share above threshold
FRAG_HIGH = reversal fragility above threshold
EXT_BREAK = severe or worsening ECT condition

Then define the qualitative regimes directly.

I would code them like this.

EXPANSION = PROF_UP * ~DYS_HIGH * ~EXT_BREAK

STAGNATION_CRISIS = PROF_DOWN * DYS_HIGH * OFF_HIGH * ~EXT_BREAK

STRUCTURAL_CRISIS = PROF_DOWN * DYS_HIGH * FRAG_HIGH * EXT_BREAK

FORCED_OFFSET = PROF_UP * RESTORE_FAIL * EXT_BREAK * (DYS_HIGH + FRAG_HIGH)

FRAGILE_RECOVERY = PROF_UP * RESTORE_FAIL * ~EXT_BREAK * FRAG_HIGH

That gives you two big crisis families and then their internal specificities.

So the logic becomes:

stagnation crisis = profitability trouble with dysfunctionality, but without full structural rupture through the external corridor

structural crisis = profitability breakdown plus high dysfunctionality/fragility plus binding external disequilibrium

forced offset = rebound without restoration, under worsening structural stress

fragile recovery = rebound that remains unstable even if the external constraint is not yet fully binding

That is already very close to Boolean algebra / csQCA language.

Then your hypothesis testing becomes much cleaner. You can build truth tables with one row per period and ask things like:

Is EXT_BREAK necessary for STRUCTURAL_CRISIS?
Is PROF_DOWN * DYS_HIGH sufficient for STAGNATION_CRISIS?
Does PROF_UP * RESTORE_FAIL * EXT_BREAK consistently produce FORCED_OFFSET?

That is much better than trying to narrate five indicators independently and hoping the reader kindly does the synthesis for you.

For the actual Chile sequence, I would provisionally map the periods like this.

1961–69 → expansion
1969–72 → structural crisis onset / breakdown
1972–74 → forced offset
1974–76 → renewed structural fragility
1976–78 → partial recovery

And inside the micro corridor:

1969–72 → breakdown
1972–74 → forced offset under worsening external pressure
1974–75 → non-sustainable slippage

That is the nested periodization that best matches the diagnostics you just built.

So the results package should now produce three new core outputs.

First, a period panel:
one row per period, continuous summaries plus Boolean versions.

Second, a classification table:
period, class, subtype, brief interpretation.

Third, a truth-table artifact:
periods as cases, Boolean conditions as columns, outcomes as crisis labels.

In file terms, I would add:

period_panel_nested.csv
period_classification_nested.csv
truth_table_structural_crisis.csv
truth_table_forced_offset.csv
truth_table_stagnation_crisis.csv

And one figure that the chapter can actually live off:
a horizontal period band showing the nested chronology with labels like expansion, breakdown, forced offset, fragile recovery.

So the narrative architecture becomes much tighter:

the diagnostics identify the motion,
the period panel collapses the motion into states,
the Boolean algebra tests the conditions,
and the written results narrate the states rather than juggling raw indicators.

That is the bridge from econometric chaos to readable political economy.

The next move should be to define the exact threshold book and build the period-state table in the results package.

but is ok a first profit swing classification 

Yes — that is a good move. ✅

A first profit-swing classification is perfectly acceptable as the outer temporal shell. It gives you the chronology. Then the dysfunctionality indices and their sources give you the inner qualitative content of each period.

That is actually the elegant sequence:

Profit swings define the periods.

Dysfunctionality composition defines what kind of period each one is.

Recapitalization and external disequilibrium tell you whether the movement is restorative, forced, fragile, or structurally blocked.

So profit swings should not be the final typology. They should be the first-pass segmentation rule.

I would freeze the first-pass profit-swing classification as:

1940–1946 — restorative expansion

1946–1949 — corrective downturn

1949–1955 — renewed expansion

1955–1961 — stagnation tendency

1961–1969 — contradictory expansion

1969–1972 — crisis breakdown

1972–1974 — forced offset

1974–1976 — structural fragility

1976–1978 — partial recovery

That is already strong enough to organize the results package.

Then, in a second layer, each period gets refined by the dysfunctionality profile. For example:

which component dominates: distribution, utilization/realization, relative prices, productive capacity, wedge

whether the period is mainly offsetting, reversal-prone, or grossly dysfunctional

whether recapitalization is strong, weak, or decoupled from profitability

whether ECT indicates an external structural bind

So the final object becomes something like:

period | profit_swing_class | dysfunctionality_profile | recapitalization_profile | external_constraint | final_class

That is the bridge from a clean empirical segmentation to the richer historical classification you want.

So yes: profit-swing classification first, dysfunctionality-based refinement second. That is the right order, and it keeps the typology from becoming arbitrary or prematurely overbuilt.


given the farmework of intersecting temporalities, we are going to run a parallel classification of distributive conflict, filtering with an HP with standard annual frequency recommendations for implementations (not remember the lambda right now) to classify the tendencies of distributive conflict and have a parallel track of the accumulation regime corridor with a parallel temporality of distributive conflict. 

Thought for 24s
Yes. That is a strong move.

Within your intersecting-temporalities framework, I would treat distributive conflict as a parallel temporal track, not as a subcomponent folded immediately into profitability. Profit swings give you the accumulation-regime corridor; distributive conflict gets its own temporal classification and then you intersect both tracks period by period.

For the HP filter, the standard annual recommendation is:

λ
=
6.25
λ=6.25
That is the annual analogue of the quarterly 1600 convention under the Ravn–Uhlig scaling rule. For annual data, 6.25 should be your baseline. I would still run a robustness pass with a second smoother setting, but 6.25 is the right default anchor.

The clean architecture is this.

First track:
profit-swing / accumulation corridor
This is your master period shell:
1940–46, 1946–49, 1949–55, 1955–61, 1961–69, 1969–72, 1972–74, 1974–76, 1976–78.

Second track:
distributive-conflict temporality
This should be built on your primitive distributive variable, so use wage share ω_t as the main carrier, not profit share as the primitive.

I would decompose ω_t into:

omega_trend

omega_cycle = omega_t - omega_trend

Then classify the distributive dynamic using both:

the sign of the cycle

the direction of movement in the cycle

That gives a much richer language than just “high” or “low.”

A good first classification is:

wage-pressure build-up: omega_cycle > 0 and rising

wage-pressure plateau: omega_cycle > 0 and flat/falling slightly

profit-restoration push: omega_cycle < 0 and falling

distributive relaxation: omega_cycle < 0 and rising back toward zero

neutral / balanced conflict: cycle close to zero

So profit periods and distributive periods are not forced to coincide. That is the point. You want exactly the possibility that:

profitability is rebounding,

while distributive conflict is intensifying,
or

profitability is falling,

while distributive pressure is being repressed.

That is where the intersecting temporality becomes analytically interesting.

I would operationalize it like this.

For each year, compute:

omega_cycle_t = omega_t - hp_trend(omega_t, lambda = 6.25)
d_omega_cycle_t = omega_cycle_t - lag(omega_cycle_t)
Then define crisp yearly states:

DIST_HIGH if omega_cycle_t > threshold

DIST_LOW if omega_cycle_t < -threshold

DIST_RISING if d_omega_cycle_t > slope_threshold

DIST_FALLING if d_omega_cycle_t < -slope_threshold

From that, define yearly conflict states:

wage_push = DIST_HIGH * DIST_RISING

high_conflict_persistent = DIST_HIGH * ~DIST_FALLING

profit_restoration = DIST_LOW * DIST_FALLING

conflict_relaxation = DIST_LOW * DIST_RISING

balanced_conflict = neither high nor low

Then collapse those year states into your master profit-swing periods by majority rule, mean cycle, or endpoint-plus-average summary.

That gives you a crosswalk table like:

period | profit_swing_class | distributive_conflict_class | recapitalization_profile | dysfunctionality_profile | external_constraint

And then the real payoff comes from the intersections:

contradictory expansion + wage_push

structural crisis + high_conflict_persistent

forced offset + profit_restoration

structural fragility + conflict_relaxation under ext_break

partial recovery + renewed wage_push

That is much better than forcing distributive conflict to be absorbed into the profitability label.

Two cautions.

First, HP has endpoint problems, especially in short windows. So estimate the HP trend on the full annual series, then read the yearly states inside your nested periodization. Do not HP-filter only the very short window unless you want a distorted last-year story.

Second, because your framework is historically contingent, the distributive-conflict classification should remain parallel, not hierarchical. In other words, do not say “the profit period is really distributive conflict.” Say instead:

this accumulation corridor intersected with this distributive-conflict temporality.

That preserves your intersecting-temporalities logic.

So the clean implementation rule is:

use profit swings for the main periodization

use HP-filtered wage-share dynamics for the parallel distributive-conflict timeline

intersect both into a joint classification table

If you want, the next step should be a concrete classification dictionary for the distributive-conflict track, with thresholds and period-collapse rules written in code-ready form.


wait, what if we used my measure of capacity utilization as filtering? or its dynamics, i.e. removing the cyclical component by the cyclical component driven by the rate of growth of capacity utilization. Thought for 26s
Yes — that can make a lot of sense, and in your framework it may actually be better than a pure HP filter.

The key distinction is this:

An HP filter gives you a statistical cycle.

Using your own capacity-utilization measure gives you an economically grounded cycle.

For your project, that second option is often stronger, because your u_t is not just another macro series. It is already a theoretically constructed object tied to effective demand, productive capacity, and the crisis corridor. So filtering distributive conflict through utilization would mean:

isolate the part of distributive movement that is just demand-pressure / utilization-driven, and separate it from the part that looks more autonomous or structurally conflictual.

That is a good idea.

But I would not phrase it as “remove the cyclical component by the rate of growth of capacity utilization” without one refinement:

the level of utilization and the change in utilization do different jobs.

u_t or ln u_t captures the state of pressure on the system.
Δu_t or Δln u_t captures the change in pressure.

For distributive conflict, the state usually matters more than the change alone. A high-utilization economy can sustain wage pressure even if utilization is no longer rising fast. So if you only use the growth rate of utilization, you may throw away the most meaningful part.

So my recommendation is:

Use capacity utilization as an economic filter, but do it in two possible ways.

econometrics becomces an issue, this is not simply an OLS regresion

Thought for 22s
Exactly. That is the problem. This is not a simple OLS regression problem.

If you regress wage share on utilization and call the residual “distributive conflict,” you are sneaking in a causal structure that the data do not justify cleanly. The issues pile up fast:

simultaneity between distribution and demand

nonstationarity / common trends

serial correlation

structural breaks

very short crisis windows

and the fact that your utilization measure is itself a constructed object, not an exogenous regressor

So yes: plain OLS would be too blunt. 🧨

The clean way to think about it is to separate three levels.

Level 1: descriptive classification
No causal claim. Just identify the distributive-conflict temporality as its own track.

Level 2: utilization-conditioned decomposition
Still not a full structural model. This is a “purged” or “conditioned” conflict measure.

Level 3: structural econometrics
A real simultaneous system. Probably too heavy for this chapter-facing classification layer.

For what you need now, I would stay at Level 1 or Level 2, not Level 3.

So I would not say:

“the residual is the true causal distributive conflict.”

I would say:

“this is the distributive movement not directly tracked by the utilization corridor under the chosen reduced-form filter.”

That is much safer and much more accurate.

My recommendation is:

Use profit swings as the outer temporal shell.
Then run a parallel distributive-conflict classification that is either:

Option A. Pure descriptive conflict track
Based on wage share dynamics alone:

level relative to trend

change in wage share

maybe cycle from HP with annual lambda = 6.25

This is the safest and lightest route.

Option B. Utilization-conditioned conflict track
But not with plain OLS in levels. Instead use something like:

decompose in stationary space

or use a small VAR/VECM residualization

or use a simple projection only as a descriptive purge, not as structural estimation

If you want the cleanest compromise, I would do this:

Build the main distributive-conflict classification from wage-share dynamics alone.

Build a secondary utilization-conditioned robustness track.

Compare both.

Only if they broadly agree, use that agreement in the final narrative.

That way the econometrics do not hijack the chapter.

So the practical rule becomes:

main chapter classification = profit swings + dysfunctionality + recapitalization + raw distributive track

robustness appendix / side table = utilization-conditioned distributive track

That is much more defensible.

If you try to make the utilization-conditioning the main measure, you risk spending pages defending an econometric identification that is not the main contribution of the chapter.

So yes: your instinct is right.
This is not “just run OLS.”
It is better handled as a parallel temporal classification problem, with econometrics kept modest and transparent rather than pretending to extract a pure structural conflict residual.

The shortest clean formulation is:

use distributive conflict as a parallel temporality first; treat utilization-conditioned filtering as a robustness refinement, not as the foundational classifier.

omega_hat_u_t = fitted distributive movement conditioned by utilization

conflict_escalation if omega_conflict_t > 0 and rising

That gives you a parallel distributive-conflict track you can intersect with the profit-swing periods.

profit swings define the periods

ARDL-filtered conflict defines the distributive temporality inside them

dysfunctionality / recapitalization / ECT refine the class

That is elegant and manageable.

because ARDL includes lagged dependent variables, the fitted value is a mix of:

utilization-driven movement

persistence in wage share itself

# Memo 1 — Collapsed Profit-Swing Periodization and Refinement Architecture

## Status
Locked for the current workflow.

This memo defines the chapter-facing collapsed periodization of Chilean profit swings for 1940–1978 and the architecture for its later refinement through dysfunctionality, recapitalization, and external constraint diagnostics.

---

## 1. Collapsed periodization of profit swings

The master periodization is fixed as:

- **1940–1946** — restorative expansion
- **1946–1949** — corrective downturn
- **1949–1955** — renewed expansion
- **1955–1961** — stagnation tendency
- **1961–1969** — contradictory expansion
- **1969–1972** — crisis breakdown
- **1972–1974** — forced offset
- **1974–1976** — structural fragility
- **1976–1978** — partial recovery

This periodization is the primary temporal shell for the profitability results package.

It is designed to satisfy three conditions simultaneously:

1. preserve the medium-run structure of profitability dynamics from 1940 onward,
2. intensify temporal resolution as the crisis corridor is approached,
3. allow the critical juncture of interest to emerge within a single nested chronology rather than through competing periodizations.

---

## 2. Interpretation rule for the collapsed periodization

This periodization is a **first-pass classification of profit swings**, not the final qualitative typology of the regime.

Its function is to provide the outer temporal shell within which more granular determinations will later be made.

That means:

- the profit swing defines the **period boundary**,
- but the qualitative content of the period will be refined by the internal composition of dysfunctionality, recapitalization, and external disequilibrium.

The periodization therefore remains necessary but not sufficient for final classification.

---

## 3. Refinement through dysfunctionality indices

Each profit-swing period will later be refined by examining the internal composition of dysfunctionality.

The refinement will ask, period by period:

- which component dominates:
  - **distribution**
  - **utilization / realization**
  - **relative prices**
  - **productive capacity**
  - **wedge**

- whether the period is mainly:
  - **offsetting**
  - **reversal-prone**
  - **grossly dysfunctional**

- whether recapitalization is:
  - **strong**
  - **weak**
  - **decoupled from profitability**

- whether the ECT indicates:
  - **no major external bind**
  - **heightened external pressure**
  - **external structural bind**

This gives the refinement layer that turns a raw profit swing into a historically specific regime movement.

---

## 4. Final classification object

The final object to be constructed in the results package is:

`period | profit_swing_class | dysfunctionality_profile | recapitalization_profile | external_constraint | final_class`

Where:

- `period` = one of the locked temporal units above,
- `profit_swing_class` = the first-pass profitability class,
- `dysfunctionality_profile` = internal composition of crisis tendencies,
- `recapitalization_profile` = reproductive closure or its weakness,
- `external_constraint` = degree and direction of external structural stress,
- `final_class` = historically specific qualitative regime label.

This architecture is preferred because it avoids collapsing historically contingent periods into a standard external typology too early. The final class must emerge from the intersection of multiple determinations, not from profitability alone.

---

## 5. Working implication for the next session

The next results-package step is not to redesign the periodization.

The next step is to build the refinement layer for each locked period using:

- profit swings as the temporal shell,
- dysfunctionality indices and their dominant source composition,
- recapitalization dynamics,
- ECT diagnostics.

Only after this refinement should the chapter-facing final qualitative labels be fixed.

---

## 6. Provisional chapter-facing reading

At the current stage, the collapsed periodization may already be read as:

- early postwar oscillation between restoration and correction,
- a long contradictory expansion culminating in the late 1960s,
- crisis breakdown beginning in 1969,
- offset and renewed fragility through the mid-1970s,
- incomplete recovery by the end of the sample.

This reading remains provisional until the dysfunctionality and recapitalization refinement is merged into the period table.

---
# Memo 2 — Parallel Corridor of Class Struggle Using an ARDL Filter Conditioned by Utilization

## Status
Locked as the parallel-temporality strategy for distributive conflict.

This memo defines the conceptual and operational rule for constructing a parallel corridor of class struggle using an ARDL filter with capacity utilization.

---

## 1. Purpose

The profitability periodization should not bear alone the full burden of historical classification.

A parallel temporal track of distributive conflict is required in order to preserve the framework of intersecting temporalities.

This second track will not replace the profit-swing chronology. Instead, it will run alongside it and later be intersected with it period by period.

Its purpose is to identify the temporality of class struggle as a distinct movement, rather than reducing it to a subcomponent of profitability.

---

## 2. Why use an ARDL filter

A static regression of wage share on utilization is inadequate.

The issue is not only correlation between distribution and utilization, but also:

- dynamic persistence in distribution,
- lagged adjustment,
- possible long-run relation between distributive variables and utilization,
- the need to distinguish long-run corridor from short-run deviations.

An ARDL is therefore used as a **filter**, not as a claim to full structural identification.

Its function is to dynamically condition distributive movement on utilization and thereby recover a parallel conflict track.

---

## 3. Core variable choice

The primitive distributive variable will be **wage share** `ω_t`.

This is preferred because:

- it aligns with the locked notation preference,
- it preserves profit share as residual,
- it provides the most direct bridge between distribution and class struggle.

Capacity utilization `u_t` or its logged form will act as the conditioning corridor.

---

## 4. Conceptual structure of the ARDL filter

The ARDL is not used here to define a generic cycle.

It is used to define a **utilization-conditioned long-run distributive corridor**.

In conceptual form:

`ω_t = f(ω lags, u lags)`

or in long-run notation:

`ω*_t = a + β u_t + deterministics`

where `ω*_t` is the long-run utilization-conditioned path of wage share.

The crucial object is not the simple regression residual by itself, but the deviation of observed wage share from the long-run corridor:

`ω_t - ω*_t`

This deviation is the preferred candidate for the parallel temporality of distributive conflict.

---

## 5. Interpretation of the filter

The utilization-conditioned long-run path captures the distributive movement that is compatible with the accumulation corridor under the estimated dynamic relation.

The deviation from that path captures distributive tension not directly absorbed by that corridor.

So the interpretation rule is:

- `ω*_t` = utilization-conditioned distributive corridor,
- `ω_t - ω*_t` = filtered distributive-conflict component.

This object should not be called simply “the cycle.”
It is better described as:

- **utilization-filtered distributive conflict**, or
- **deviation from the long-run distributive corridor**.

This terminology is preferred because it is theoretically tighter and avoids confusion with purely statistical decomposition language.

---

## 6. Role within the intersecting-temporalities framework

The distributive-conflict corridor is a **parallel temporality**, not a subordinate layer inside profitability.

That means the workflow becomes:

1. profit swings define the primary temporal shell,
2. the ARDL filter defines the parallel distributive-conflict temporality,
3. both are later intersected period by period.

The goal is to identify whether a given profitability phase coincides with:

- rising distributive pressure,
- persistent distributive conflict,
- profit-restoration pressure,
- conflict relaxation,
- or a more neutral distributive alignment.

This preserves the relational logic of intersecting temporalities.

---

## 7. Practical implementation rule

The ARDL filter should be estimated on the full available annual sample used for the profitability analysis.

The filtered distributive-conflict component should then be summarized within the locked profit-swing periods.

This is preferred to estimating separate short-window filters, because short windows are too fragile and too sensitive to endpoint issues.

So the workflow is:

- estimate ARDL on full annual sample,
- recover the long-run distributive corridor,
- compute the deviation of observed wage share from that corridor,
- classify the resulting distributive-conflict movement inside each profit-swing period.

---

## 8. Deliverable architecture for the next session

The next session should produce:

1. a yearly series of:
   - observed wage share,
   - utilization-conditioned long-run wage-share corridor,
   - filtered distributive-conflict deviation,

2. a collapsed period table aligned to the locked profit-swing periodization,

3. a parallel classification of distributive conflict for each period.

This classification will later be merged with:

- dysfunctionality profiles,
- recapitalization profiles,
- external constraint diagnostics.

No Boolean algebra testing is required at this stage.

---

## 9. What is deferred

The following are explicitly deferred to a later merge stage:

- Boolean algebra testing,
- necessary/sufficient condition analysis,
- final truth-table construction,
- formal integration into hypothesis-testing logic.

For now, the task is only to construct the parallel distributive-conflict corridor and align it to the profit-swing shell.

---

## 10. Bottom line

The chapter will proceed with two parallel temporal tracks:

- a **profit-swing corridor of accumulation dynamics**,
- a **utilization-filtered corridor of distributive conflict**.

These will later be intersected to refine the historical classification of crisis, stagnation, offset, fragility, and recovery.

This keeps the empirical strategy aligned with the framework of intersecting temporalities while avoiding premature collapse into a single standard typology.

---
